This period is the great dumbing down.

Apr 19, 2024

I’ve been thinking about how to frame this time period we are in. A time after a great wave of illness. Indeed we are still in that great wave, even if you aren’t hearing about it from your government or on the news. This is step one.

And then with step two we have this “magic tool” that has been sold to so many as a panacea of knowledge, a way to level the field. Except its effect will have the exact opposite result. It will not level the field but increase disparity.

It won’t replace menial jobs, it won’t create high quality, high paying, high reward employment for folks. No, menial jobs will only increase, and with them the need to work more of them. Hard and unforgiving jobs. Jobs that make you scrape the barrel.

And that is step three. When your needs aren’t met, you can’t think critically. You don’t see big pictures, you see what is in front of you to get you to whatever is the next thing.

Apr 19, 2024

It’s just the same boring playbook as every other quick trick trend that came before and it will burn out and burn up and take jobs and ruin lives just like the ones that came before until the capitalists find some new trick to throw their money at. So boring and dumb.

Yep, I’m talking about AI.

It is impossible to read this and square it with living in a world that wants to continue spreading and catching Covid with abandon.

Here is the result of my hard work this week.

Apr 18, 2024

And why I am pretty much laid up today. Two years ago, I removed the grass behind the berm from just beyond where it ended near the new basalt rock pathway from the sideyard to the patio. That was such a success that I decided to finish removing the remaining strip this year to round out the lawn in the backyard and be completely rid of narrow grass paths.

This section proved much harder the strip behind the berm, I think due to the proximity to trees and roots. I removed the sod in four strips, two strips a day for two days. And then on the third day I had my neighbor bring me a few wheelbarrows of top soil the he’d removed from his front yard to put in some drains and rock paths. It was a perfect situation. Finally, I topped the soil with four wheelbarrows of mulch and tamped it down. This turned out exactly as I had hoped it would, and now the path from the grass and around the berm in what I call “the woodland” is complete.

In a lot of ways this is the continuation of that project I started two years ago, after the completion of a basalt stepping stone path in the sideyard. I don’t publish to Substack anymore, but you can read about that project here: Behind the Berm.

The gentians are in their prime.

Apr 18, 2024

These are gentiana acaulis (unsure of variety, though I probably have a tag in the garage), aka trumpet gentian. I remember my mom having gentians in her garden. Once my sister was weeding as a chore and accidentally dug some of them up and threw them out (they were not in bloom). My mom had a bit of a fit about it.

I suppose I’d do the same. These are in my front yard terraces, the top terrace next to the lawn. The bottom terrace is next to the sidewalk and anyone walking by is about eye-level to these intense blue blooms.

POSSE copies:

I have a yard. No, I have a garden.

Apr 18, 2024

You might notice I talk or post about it a bit. I share photos. I am proud of my garden. Every single plant in it I put there. What used to be empty terraces in the front and lawn all around, is now a mature and varied garden with interesting microclimates and “rooms”. This took thought, patience, and dedication.

Gardens need places for the eye to rest. Moments of silence in the physical landscape. Sometimes this takes shape with a lawn. People hate lawns because they use water and chemicals. But lawns still provide a purpose and if used in moderation I still feel have their place in the garden.

In my garden there are only two small areas of lawn remaining. I removed all of the rest of the lawn, approximately 2/3rds of the total lawn that used to make up my yard is now landscaped garden beds designed by me. But that remaining lawn does require irrigation. Had there not already been lawn and irrigation here when I bought this house, it is likely there never would have been.

In the city of Portland you are required to maintain an irrigation system. This might or might not mean you hire someone to do that. But at a minimum someone licensed to do so must perform a backflow test, and this usually coincides with the spring startup of the system. For me this occurred on Tuesday this week, and I had the guy perform a couple tweaks to my system.

One of those tweaks was to the controller. Six or so years ago I had a weather system put in that is connected to my irrigation controller. It is just a little device that collects rain water and tips it out when it gets to a certain point, takes temperature readings, etc. and stores all of that data in the controller and tells it when the different zones of my garden need water.

I have four zones, only two of them are lawn, the two areas mentioned above. The remaining two are drip for some of the newer areas of garden beds where I provide drip emitters directly to a plant’s roots. Now you may be wondering why I am telling this backstory about my yard, garden, irrigation, lawn, etc. Here’s why.

My neighborhood has a “healthy” raccoon population. I’ve witnessed entire families traveling through my yard. I’ve seen momma’s with five kits scaling a fence. I’ve see a momma with a single kit in the middle of the day! But mostly I see the aftermath of raccoons in my yard. And of that aftermath is what happens during the summer when it is hot and the irrigation runs late at night/in the middle of the night and the raccoons decide to have a party.

It is not a pretty sight. It is a mess. They damage plants, they dig holes, they cause mayhem. Last year when the irrigation guy came out I asked them to change the controller to run the irrigation in the morning not at night because of the raccoons. I watched the guy get into the controller and seemingly perform the modifications for this request. However, it was not really fixed. I attempted again, I had tried before, to navigate this controllers settings and menus, and alas dear reader, this system is too complicated for me, an unusual thing to admit.

So last year I got up every day during the summer that I ran the irrigation (not every day) at 5am and manually ran it to avoid the Rowdy Raccoon Rave in the garden. I did this for four long months, basically May-September. It wasn’t fun, but I didn’t feel like calling the irrigation guy back, which would have incurred a charge and I just wasn’t in the mood to tell this guy that he did his job wrong.

This year it was a different guy and he fully admitted the controller is far more complicated than it needs to be, that even he had a hard time figuring it out, and that he tried to make the changes but was unsure, and that if I have issues or it isn’t running when I want it to to call him back. He even said he might have to send his supervisor to figure the controller out. I have to tell you I feel so much better about myself after that conversation. And last night, well, this morning, guess what? The system ran at the right time! I was making coffee and it started at 5:15am just like he said it would! I am elated, you don’t understand, this is so great.

Apr 18, 2024

Today's featured photo from the Photos app (2024/04/14)

Apr 14, 2024

This tree is yet another of my Japanese Maple survivors. I started a draft on Substack when I was still writing there in 2022 about my other survivor and never finished it. Maybe I should move it here.

I nearly killed this tree last year when I took a hose from the driveway to water it. The hose had been laying on the concrete all morning and picked up solar gain, superheating the water inside. I wasn’t thinking and almost immediately realized what I had done but it was too late.

Over the course of the next few days to weeks, the tree lost nearly all its leaves, but later pushed out new growth into the summer. I didn’t know what was truly dead so I waited for it to bud out this spring and pruned off everything that had no signs of growth. I lost about half the canopy. But it lived. It has the most spectacular fall color.

üìù From Apple Annie’s Weblog

2024-04-12

Garden Status (2024/04/11)

Apr 11, 2024

It has been about a month, maybe a little less, since the last Garden Status and we’re getting into the thick of spring. Everything is popping! I grabbed some photos this week, so here’s a slew!

There are three aubrietas in the front yard terraces and next to retaining walls that are as lovely as can be this year. The candy tuft (not pictured) is also more full of blooms than I can remember in years past. My neighbor tells me these plants really like a good long vernal period and we haven’t been having those much in recent years (probably due to climate change), but this year’s deep intense 14-15¬∞F freeze in January must have done the trick for them.

There is no end to the joy the pansies, violas, and primroses, bring me each fall/winter/spring. If my climate allowed, I’d grow them all year. But in about a month, the temperatures will not longer be conducive to them thriving and I’ll be swapping them out for heat-loving summer annuals. Enjoy them while you can!

The Deshojo Japanes Maple tree on the patio is fantastic this year. It’s had a rough couple years, and I considered it being time to move it out of the container and into the ground. Unfortunately this would not happen in my garden because: a) I don’t have the room for another tree in my garden, and b) I have had a Japanese maple succumb to Verticillium wilt in my garden, and other than the two Bloodgoods in the parking strip, which are quite mature and not showing any signs yet, I don’t want to take the chance on any others. I lost a Crimson Queen and it crushed me. So, when this tree needs to get out of its container, it will leave my garden and end up elsewhere.

This tree will transition the leaves to all-green by summer time, and then back to a rainbow of hues and brilliant reds and oranges in the fall. This bright pinky-red color only lasts for a brief fleeting moment in the spring. It really is one of the best Japanese maples for color changing leaves.

The common name of this plant is “bog rosemary” but it isn’t a rosemary, and it isn’t even closely related to rosemary. Bog rosemary is more closely related to ericaceous evergreen shrubs such as huckleberry, blueberry, and cranberry. The name comes from the rosemary-esque leaves, though upon closer inspection they resemble tiny rhododendron leaves, also a relative, and its tolerance and preference for boggy growing conditions‚Äîdon’t let it dry out!

I don’t often post pictures of the weeping white spruce (Picea Glauca ‘Pendula’) because it is sandwiched between two other trees and hard to get on its own. It usually is included in more expansive pictures of my entire backyard. But this year the tree is producing cones! Little red cones, oodles of them at the top of the tree, though I see signs of them farther down, so I’ll need to get some pictures of them too once they develop. I got up on a ladder to get these pictures üòÅ

And the final set of pictures are of a narrow upright crabapple in the back corner of my yard called ‘Marilee’. This sweet little tree produces the most adorable bright pink buds followed by classic pinky-white apple blossoms with yellow starburst centers. And they cover the branches in what appear like sleeves of blossoms.

Some Day Notes (2024/04/06)

Apr 6, 2024

A month has gone by since my last note‚Äîwhere did the time go?! Much of it has been spent struggling internally over how to spend my time: web tinkering or gardening. Since spring is well upon us in western Oregon, I have a lot to do on both fronts.

We avoided a late freeze this year so the magnolia tree has been in one of the most abundant and log-lasting blooms (super bloom?) of any year since I planted it more than ten years ago. Over the past week I’ve been mulching the garden, a little bit at a time. I’m about 2/3rds done, but most of the work will be in the backyard where I need to rake up some magnolia petals in the rockery before spreading mulch and I’ll be removing some sod in the back corner of the garden to round out the lawn. I’m planning on using some of the sod to fill a few holes elsewhere.

On the web, I am keeping up a good cadence with blog posts, both here on Micro.blog and on weblog. I’m still working on themes.lol regularly and keeping the homepage set to show the most recent updates. On 3x5.pics a new index card is published every four days. I purchased a new domain (tableforone.cafe) and plan to use a second microblog and custom theme for it. But first, I want to get an initial release of my styles on themes.lol wrapped.

Enough of the preamble, onward!

  • I’ve carried on with my featured photos but noted a change to how I curate them in a post.
  • I wrote a small response to a piece published by NPR regarding continued vigilance by chronically ill and vulnerable folks.

  • I joined the IndieWeb webring on this microblog, the first I’ve joined here. I have several on weblog, and I’d like to join more!

  • I’m still thinking about cross-posting, I still haven’t set anything up. I think I will have better momentum on this soon.
  • I discovered thehtml.review.

    • Sigh. I just have zero trust in any goodwill from this company ever.

I am on a quest for an answer.

Apr 3, 2024

I’m prepared not to get one. I’m prepared not to be satisfied by the ones that I get. But I’ve been bothered by this thing long enough now I’m asking it.

If you share photos anywhere: on Mastodon/Pixelfed/etc, on your own website, on some other public platform where other people have access to it, and you don’t add alt text for images, why?

I really cannot understand the lack of empathy behind it. I’ve heard every manner of excuse, including the sometimes draining effects for people with cognitive or other limiting factors from writing the text. I actually have those factors. Part of my illness is cognitive limitations and I have to be mindful of them when I decide to take something on. If I don’t think I can complete the thing with the necessary requirements, I don’t undertake the thing. That includes posting a photo. I will put it off if I can’t add alt text for other people who also have limiting factors.

My consternation at the lack of alt text I encounter day-to-day is most disturbing when it is done by someone who absolutely knows better: an author who writes about typography! It is such a jolt to witness, a dichotomy that makes me never want to purchase anything he creates. I find it so sad and bizarre and I can’t come up with a meaning other than apathy.

If you have another reason, I’d love to hear it. If you try to add alt text but sometimes forget or fail, I’d love to know. I need some faith in humanity restored here.

My ME Life: my last job (part one)

Mar 30, 2024

Since the first actual post in this series, “some early childhood”, my brain went to my last job. So, I’m obviously jumping around quite a bit. I think there are several reasons for this. Nothing is a straight line, and most definitely not in my life. I think some parts of my life have had larger influences on the whole, and then of course there are contemporary events that make me think back to certain periods. My last job is one of them, as I’m still reeling from that time period.

I was working at what was supposed to be my dream job. I had left the job prior to that feeling dissatisfied and taken for granted. During my annual review I came prepared with my accomplishments, strengths, and plans for the next year, coupled with demands for a merit/salary increase. While they agreed to the first part of the equation, they did not agree to the second. So, I went packing and applied like a “cold call” to a place that I had always admired, a place I thought of as a pinnacle in the open source community I was a part of.

When I put in my notice at the other place, guess what happened? Yeah, they offered me the salary I had asked for. Too late, my dream job offered me a 12% increase over that! But as with most things you place on a pedestal, they rarely live up to the ideals you imagined, and my dream job ended spectacularly. Over the years, and especially in the immediate aftermath, I thought I should write a book about the experience. I guess whatever I write here will have to serve as that now.

It was Labor Day weekend and we all got notice to be in the office by 9am the following week for an important announcement. This email came in during the holiday weekend, if I recall correctly. It may have actually made reference to a “big new project”. The big new project? The business was shuttering. But what happened when we returned to the office from the weekend went even further.

Not only was the business shuttering, but the middle management had known about this for some time and were doing all they could to save us, the workers, from having to scramble to find jobs on short notice, and, possibly worse, compete with each other applying to similar places. The work we did on the platform we used could very well end up that way. But I think how it actually went may have added insult to injury.

We were faced with what I can only describe as a panel of executives. If that makes you want to cry, well, yes, I did some crying later that day. For all of the “oh shit” feelings this dug up in me, having left a job only a year earlier after feeling unappreciated and then only after threatening to leave was told “yeah, sure we’ll pay you what you think you are worth”, this was bringing up a lot of bad feelings. I had come to this company with stars in my eyes, a company whose tagline was “Technology for Good” and I’d spent a year working on a new platform for AmeriCorps VISTA.

This panel of executives was from a company based in Washington, DC, and they worked on giant platforms (using the same software we did) but it was anything but technology for good. Even before acquiring the dream job, this company had opened an office in Portland and garnered a reputation for paying high salaries but expecting workers to trash their work/life balance. I felt cornered, to put it mildly. The panel was there for the week, and they would be interviewing us all as an on-the-spot job application, so to speak. No, I’m not joking. The next day I came in and was put into a small room with two guys, one I sort of knew from the tech meetup scene, and the other one was one of the owners of the company from DC.

The interview left me feeling all the things: imposter syndrome, like all my eggs were in this one basket, was I stuck in some contract that prevented me from looking elsewhere? Of course, you could choose not to apply and just finish out the month at our current company, as that is what the arrangement was: the current company would shutter at the end of September. You would interview with the new company, and if approved for a position, would spend that month “working” for them on a contract basis. Then we would all find out at the beginning of October if we had permanent full-time positions with them. It was hell. I felt like I was living on pins and needles for a month. It was like an ouf-of-body experience. I had to put feelers out there and see what other positions were viable lest I find myself hanging without a hope in a month.

And I did that, but I didn’t actually end up finding an alternative. What I did do was build up a repository of information to come armed with if and when they gave me a job offer. I was surprised that it paid off and they gave me the salary I asked for. I took the job with the new company from DC and would be starting in their brand new office in The Pearl along with the fourteen other team members that were also coming on board, plus their existing staff that had been previously crammed into a tiny “coat closet of an office” in SE Portland, as well as anyone else from the company from across the country that would be moving to join us.

To be continued.

Mar 27, 2024

I don’t know what this looks like yet, but I’ve been really upset with some of the conversations around Threads and the Fediverse. I need to organize my head, internalize some of the discussion, and really just keep to myself and finish writing some blog posts and pages I really want to finish. I do not envy what many Mastodon admins are grappling with right now. One of my favorite people on the internet, Adam of omg.lol, is a Mastodon admin on social.lol and watching him internally (and externally) feel tortured by this has upset me. I’m upset enough by my situation in life right now. How society has already placed constraints on my freedom and ability to thrive while a very real threat in virus form continues to circulate and cause disease, death, and disability. Another realism people just don’t want to deal with.

So, I’m stepping back in little bits. I will write my words in my own spaces. But I need some distance from all the conversations that are upsetting me “out there”. I don’t feel like I’m making progress in finding a medium of agreement and I don’t have the energy with the day-to-day of my illness to continue to get upset.

Take care of yourselves, and each other. Have empathy and be as kind as you can. You don’t know everyone’s circumstances.

March 14, 2015

I made a fantastic soup yesterday.

Mar 13, 2024

I had something in mind, I searched for a recipe to work from (just to get some type of proportions right), and then threw in what I had on hand.

It is a ditalini vegetable soup with:

  • 1 onion, chopped
  • 1 very large carrot, chopped
  • about 1 1/2 celery stalks, chopped
  • 4-5 garlic cloves, finely chopped
  • 1/4 cup olive oil
  • 1 15-oz can cannellini beans, drained/rinsed
  • 1 28-oz can whole tomatoes, with sauce (do not drain)‚Äîcrush in pot with masher/back of wooden spoon
  • 1 large head of broccoli, cut into small florets
  • 1 package frozen peas
  • 6-8 cups vegetable stock (I used half water, you could probably use all water)
  • 1/2 package ditalini pasta (about 1/2 pound)
  • a combination of, I didn’t measure, but about 1/2 to 1 teaspoon each:
    • Italian seasoning
    • dried parsley
    • dried basil
    • dried thyme
    • bay leaf
    • red pepper flakes
    • kosher salt (to taste)
    • freshly ground black pepper (to taste)

I think that is it…I might have missed something, I’ll add it here if I remember anything more. You could add zucchini, baby spinach, brussels sprouts, it’s a pretty versatile base. Substitute the cannellini for chickpeas or other canned bean. You could leave out the pasta entirely, though it does help thicken it up, perhaps try pearled barley instead (will take extra time to cook, might need to add it in with the liquid at the 30-minute simmer step).

Basically, sweat the first four ingredients with the olive oil, then add the rest, except for the ditalini. Cover and simmer for 30 minutes or so. Add ditalini and continue to cook about eight more minutes. Turn off burner and let sit for another 20 minutes. Serve with fresh grated parmesan.

I'm not going to name any names.

Mar 12, 2024

Perhaps especially on the IndieWeb there is a pretty heavy bias on male (and white) perspectives. I’m seeing this in who is included in some popular email newsletters when there are equal and earlier published representations of the same content by non-male authors, and also in who is being included in blogrolls.

I can’t say I’m not disappointed even if I’m not shocked. I am an aware female in this world, I live every day so this is unfortunately par for the course.

I will say that this is exactly why I chose to spin my blogroll. I wanted to be conscientious of who gets added, when they’re added, and what the make-up of the set is at the time I add it. Of course, this takes time and thought and that’s a lot more effort than some may want to put into it. I also wanted to include blogs that are new to me and that contain content outside of my usual circle.

The IndieWeb deserves better. We all deserve better. Broaden your horizons, folks. It is 2024 and you know what type of forces are out there on the rise. You can easily fight back against it by raising voices different than your own.

A response to that ableist NPR piece today.

Mar 11, 2024

I barely made it through the first two paragraphs. I definitely didn’t give it any more attention than that because I knew what it centered: an ableist attitude that prevails in media and politics right now and shuts out so many disabled and chronically ill people from every day life.

NPR‚Äôs decision to platform a piece about the difficulty of navigating life with a spouse who can‚Äôt dine indoors, instead of a piece about the difficulty of navigating a society that has made dining indoors unsafe for vulnerable groups, is just that- a decision, and a political one. It is part of an ongoing effort to cast those who cannot play along with the ‚Äúback to normal‚Äù fantasy- those who are being harmed and killed by it- as weird, paranoid, crazy, annoying, and ‚Äúthe problem.‚Äù

‚Äî Disabled people’s exclusion from indoor spaces is a civil rights violation, not an annoyance

The Featured Photos is evolving.

Mar 11, 2024

In the beginning of this adventure, it really was a daily featured photo that the Photo app on my iPad chose. But that has become less reliable and more redundant. I find myself seeking out photos that I am reminded of or if something unrelated has me looking back through time and I happen upon an image I want to use.

As mentioned recently, I am now compiling a list in Notes, a more curated list. This may mean I choose several images from the same trip. It might just mean a few of them are from the same year as I’ve seen them closely together while scrolling through my Library. Either way, it is less random and more intentional.

Perhaps this is meaningless to you. Just know that they are no longer chosen by an algorithm in an app.

Some Day Notes (2024/03/09)

Mar 9, 2024

Back for another some day note. Somewhat on track for my two week target, perhaps two-and-a-half weeks this time. Hey, that’s the point of “some day!” And speaking of notes, I have some “notes” for you this round üòâ

Every time I get to one of these I have to rewind my life and try to remember what the heck I did, where I went, what might be noteworthy‚Äîthere’s that word “note” again, I can’t escape it‚Äîand I find myself using my blog posts across my now numerous blogs to retrace the steps I’ve taken. This is probably an obvious side affect of having a blog (or two, or three…) but something I hadn’t considered. I might really appreciate this some day and it makes me want to retain this data even more when looking at my blogs from that perspective.

Here we go!

  • I spent a fair amount of time working on weblog, including checking several todo items off my ever-growing list. Something that came up spur-of-the-moment was adding a fun little web component that takes the URL to a Mastodon post and outputs a blockquote of the post with tallies of the interactions on the post (repost/reply/favorite). This is especially useful for Mastodon posts that share a blog post, as putting this at the end of your blog post serves as a “Discuss on Mastodon” prompt in lieu of comments or Webmentions, which is a whole other topic touched on briefly in this post.
  • A little while back (mid-February) a post of mine made it into the UMN web design newsletter. This gets posted to Mastodon every time including all the authors who were included and I ended up getting a mention here on Micro.blog. But a little while later, it disappeared from my mentions. I have no idea what happened, but I wanted to enshrine it for posterity in a post.
  • The February Fakeout completely took me this year and spring has come to my garden, though trepidatiously proceeding as March takes hold.
  • More work on weblog included creating a Domain Map, which was something I wanted to do instead of a “sitemap” since my domain is a suite and not just one site. Here’s a write-up.
  • After adding the “Discuss on Mastodon” component to weblog, I compared the interaction options with microblog and determined they have great parity.
  • I am the queen of series, apparently, and I can’t leave well enough alone! I added yet another part to my microformats series, this time about marking up recipes and here’s a recipe I just added after sharing a picture of the cake, Pumpkin Bundt Cake with Cinnamon Glaze.
  • Of course, I had more to say about AI stuff:
    • I shared a quote and bookmark for The Cost of a Tool
    • I lamented on the introduction of AI browser summary tools
    • More on the sour vibes AI has on the current state of the web and how it makes me feel
    • A Mastodon quote and bookmark that summarizes the AI asthetICK
    • A quote and link to a post in reaction to a recent article about AI and accessibility
  • And perfect timing for this one after all that AI stuff: a new series I’m calling Little Bright Spot. I’ll be using this when I need to cheer myself up or at least take some focus off all the bad stuff.
  • Back on weblog, I took the Blogroll for a second spin.
  • I resumed work on themes.lol:
    • On styles, I wrote about adding color swatches and continuing work on HTML element styling and added a Style List landing page.
    • On custom, I wrote a post about customizing weblog header and created a post archive page.
    • On themes, I published a March update.
  • After writing about technical things and doing technical work, I sometimes lose the motivation for blogging about interests and life, and I find inspiration hits me at the wrong time.
  • After two spins of the Blogroll + the initial set, I reviewed a trend in blog names.
  • I wrote a little ranty post about services that force users onto “choose account” pages even when there is only one user account.
  • I upgraded to Micro.blog premium for several reasons, not immediately to be used, but something I had been dragging my feet on for a while. I found that existing bookmarks don’t appear to archive? I’m not sure if that’s a bug or something that is expected. I began using the Notes feature for tracking my featured photos series and using it to organize and plan ahead for the posts.
  • I published a first post in the series My ME Life.
  • There was a point within the last week that I realized that now that I have Micro.blog premium, and I already have five active omg.lol weblogs, I have the potential for ten blogs‚Äîhow many blogs is too many blogs? I also have nine sites (not all blogs) using Tinylytics right now.
  • And finally, back to that “note” thing I was hinting at, I finally got 3x5.pics setup, designed, and mostly in a good place while I continue to move things around and make it what I want.

And that’s longer than a note, so long that Micro.blog’s preview threw a 414 Request-URI Too Large for previewing üòÜ I think that is my cue to end it here. Take care and have a great week!

April 9, 2017

3x5.pics is now a thing.

Mar 8, 2024

A while back I got a hair-brained idea to create a notes blog that was to be pictures of notes on 3x5 cards. I think I got this idea after seeing @petebrown post several photos of notes on 3x5 cards and I commented on how I loved the format. I also asked permission to use it as an idea for a new blog. Pete didn’t seem have a problem with it.

Soon after I bought a new omg.lol address during one of Adam’s sales, I think it was during the holiday/end of year sale. That was quickly followed by acquiring a new matching domain: 3x5.pics. And then life happened, and I took time off from doing much of anything on my blogs for the second half of December and nearly all of January.

February I dedicated to doing some work and posting on Apple Annie’s Weblog and catching up on in-progress work for themes.lol. Then this past week, just within the last three days, I started brainstorming and working with some design ideas. I went searching for the perfect 3x5 notecard online and was prepared to shell out for some new pens to get just the right ink-on-paper feel, but I was less than satisfied with the notecards I was finding. They were either bright white or brightly colored pastel, and the lines were also too bright. I had in my mind a sort of off-white card with faded lines, which I found a similar feeling to with the sort of chambray blue cards that feel kind of vintage.

Eventually I started working with color. I had already commissioned a nerdy bird with black-rimmed glasses and a number two pencil from @heyheymomo and used the colors as a jumping off point for my palette. I worked with the color scale generator I used for themes.lol and came up with a scale for each main color that I could work off of if I needed to go up or down the scale to ensure proper contrast between text and background.

I initially landed on six colors but ended up incorporating two additional colors because instead of taking pictures of 3x5 notecards, I created 3x5 notecards with HTML and CSS. The two additional colors are: an alternative blue to the main blue, two steps lighter on the scale, which became the background color of the notecard; and a dark burgundy that I pulled from the outlines of the nerdy bird and that became the main text color.

So even though the initial idea has morphed, I am enjoying the direction I have gone, and though perhaps a TLD like .notes might be more appropriate than .pics that domain doesn’t exist and 3x5.blog is more money than I want to sink in a side project for fun. I still think I can spin the .pics aspect of it.

I’m still considering sources for content‚Äîwhat will be the text for these cards? am I the sole author?‚Äîas at one point I thought I might solicit contributions from some.pics that would allow me to take advantage of the community moderation so that I wouldn’t be getting a bunch of junk. Since these aren’t “pics” that idea is sort of out. Though I also had the idea to generate pictures of each notecard to use as the HTML meta tag image and post to the @3x5@social.lol account that comes with my omg.lol address.

I’m also considering a submission form and/or submission by email. Both of these would require far more moderation on my end and might open up a gate I’d quickly want to close. For now, it is a single note on the homepage, the latest note, and I am writing them to be timely yet vague in content. I made an archive of all notes and a credits page to list the tools being used. I’ve also got a todo list (I have so many todo lists!) with more tweaks and improvements and mostly underneath-the-hood of weblog configuration. But so far, this has been such a fun little project to spin out in a few days.

Update: I have set up the @3x5@social.lol account and added notecard images for meta tags. I didn’t get my nerdy bird aligned quite right so it is party cut off on the bottom but the next one will be right!

Update 2: I published a new post on weblog on the creation of 3x5.pics, more about the design and CSS and how the site is now working and even some updates I made today.

My ME Life: some early childhood

Mar 7, 2024

Part one of this journey, I have no idea how this will go or how cohesive I will manage to make it. I fear I might jump around a bit until I find a rhythm, so I apologize for that. Of course, I think this will get better as time goes on, not only because I’ll get more used to writing about this stuff, but I’ll also be getting closer in time to what I recall more easily.

I’m GenX, a mid-70s baby, just barely missed the US’s bicentennial. My birthday also falls just short of Christmas. Apparently I came home in a stocking. I was a big baby and a very fast grower as an infant and toddler. You know how families do the measure-on-the-wall thing with a line? I passed up my sister in grade school. She is five years older than me.

I remember being 5 foot 4 inches in fourth grade. By the time I left elementary school I was already nearly 5 foot 8 inches. I started playing basketball in fifth grade. We had those grade school fitness tests every year and from fourth grade on I beat everyone, even the guys, at the running event. I didn’t start running for sport until junior high, but I was also a long distance cyclist and backpacker for quite a while with my father, uncles, and cousins. More on this as this series continues.

My older sister resented me from the beginning and that relationship has never improved. When I was born we lived in a neighborhood in town with lots of neighbors and other kids to play with. I have a few early memories from that time period. Things like a small creek running along the side of our property, and a tree with a rope swing, as well as a rustic split-wood fence.

The garage had a small dirty bathroom in it and I can recall being out there at least a few times. The bathroom in the house had dusty pink fixtures, I remember taking baths in the bathtub. Off the back side of the house was a family room addition with a free-standing wood fireplace, one of those black metal jobs that were very popular from about the late ’60s through 1980s. I spent a lot of time in the family room, it was where I had all my toys and the time living in that house was all pre-school, even pre-preschool and kindergarten.

The friends we had there were mostly my sisters since I was so little (<2 years old) but I still remember a few of them. One lady used to babysit us, name was Kelley, and we have a cookie recipe that we used to make called Kelley Cookies. There was a family of boys down the way that we used to play with too, and at the end of the road was a large erratic, common in this part of the country, either from volcanic activity locally or from being washed down from the Missoula Floods along the Columbia River. We’d play on that hillside in the dirt and mud all the time and make a mess of ourselves. In fact, there are pictures of me from that time eating dirt, mud, and rocks.

Maybe that’s what is wrong with me.

Many services are doing this.

Mar 5, 2024

And I must tell you, dear service: I hate it. Have you considered the possibility of a sole human living in a home? With no other humans sharing services and devices? Has that ever crossed your mind? Warning: this gets a little ranty.

Some time in the recent past, all the services added the “multi account” options to their apps, sites, services, etc. and suddenly single-user setups, those that have ever only had one user since the beginning of the service, all the way to back to before you could add multiple users, are being constantly prompted to choose the user! I am so tired of this game. Netflix is doing this. Amazon is doing this. YouTube is doing this. THERE IS NO OTHER USER, JUST DEFAULT TO THE SINGLE USER THAT HAS ALWAYS USED THIS SERVICE.

If they don’t want to automatically do this, there should at least be a setting that says: only one user, or disable adding a second account, or bypass the choose user screen, or something! This happens so often, and sometimes, I kid you not, when trying to resume a paused show on Netflix, it will interrupt the action and suddenly refresh the app and take me to the choose user screen!

I don’t know what the point of this is. Whether the services are so desperate for user data that they want to constantly force you to think about who is watching the service? like, oh I forgot! d’oh! there are many people watching! No! There is only one person here and there will only ever be one person here! Let me make that a preference please!

The motivation to blog sometimes hits at the wrong time.

Mar 4, 2024

I was laying in bed reading blogs last night on my phone. I’ll say I was trying to fall asleep, but who honestly stares at a bright rectangle and means they’re trying to fall asleep. I probably bookmarked three or four blog posts that felt inspiring or had threads I wanted to untangle in my own post. But this morning the urge is gone and I’m just here now talking about untimely motivation.

I worked too much on my computer over the weekend and my eyes feel fatigued today. I rolled out another blogroll set on weblog with accompanying “spin” post and I updated all of the styles on themes.lol to include the color variants and light and dark theme tokens. I wrote three posts and a page over there. So in all I wrote four blog posts, created one landing page (oh, right, I started another!), and updated a blogroll. And yet here I am whining about blogging motivation.

Often what I do is start a Draft with at least a working title, a small outline, or list of links to what I’m thinking about for the post. I might do that today, dig out the bookmarks I added and get some posts outlined in Drafts. But I already have a growing list of in-progress drafts to finish and can’t seem to find the motivation to do so. Why is that? Why are some posts so hard to complete? I want nothing more than to wrap up my Weblog Publishing Workflow post. It’s like a chain around my neck at this point, dragging me down every time I think about it. I don’t need new blog post ideas, I already have blog post ideas, I just need to write them!

Perhaps drawing a line in the sand is what I need. It sounds punishing, but what if I tell myself I am not allowed to start or write another blog post until at least the workflow post is published? The last time I had this chain around my neck was before NaBloPoMo and I had two gargantuan (in my mind) posts in progress, both turned into series and have been quite popular according to Tinylytics. Does Weblog Publishing Workflow need to be a series? Maybe that is what is holding me up, I need to break it apart into concrete steps so that my mind will wrap around the complexity. Hmm.

Well, here we are, at the end of another unplanned blog post about my problems with blog posts, and having ideas, starting them, following through on them, and feeling terrible about motivations in the process. Ahh such is blogging life. What a life it is.

January 3, 2016

Post interactions between microblog and weblog.

Feb 27, 2024

Today I updated the text on the “Conversation on Micro.blog” link to “Discuss on Micro.blog” to better match the perceived functionality of the new “Discuss on Mastodon” web component I added to weblog posts.

Both blogs have a “Reply by email” link as well and now non-email interactions, though not exactly the same, will both follow the pattern of taking the user (replier who wishes to “discuss”) to the intended/desired platform I wish for them to discuss on for each blog platform.

The real difference still being that Micro.blog will add the discussion to the post (webmentions) and weblog will not, it will stay on Mastodon. But I think this is an acceptable difference, even when considering my choice not to put webmentions on weblog at this time.

I read a recent post by Tantek with even more spelled out thoughts and considerations regarding all of this. The primary difference I see right now between Micro.blog and weblog is that Micro.blog users, and perhaps people interacting with them, expect that replies will show up as a conversation on a post. The only caveat to this is when a Micro.blog post makes its way to a platform to like Mastodon, by POSSE/cross-posting, and someone there replies and their responses make their way onto the post on Micro.blog. I don’t have a great solution to that right now, since this is built into the platform. But it may be okay if we consider that both Micro.blog and Mastodon use compatible protocols and weblog does not.

I feel like I’m in a good spot right now on this, and I will absolutely keep my eye on how things evolve. I remain open to adding webmentions to weblog in the future if implementation can take consent and data impermanence into account.

Spring has come to my garden.

Feb 25, 2024

I don’t put much faith in the whole groundhog’s day business over here on the west coast. We have our own indicators. In my garden that begins with planting primroses to accompany the overwintering pansies and violas in my patio containers.

This year I also bought a pot of daffodils in a lovely butter yellow color. The corona is a bit darker, but so far the unopened bud form is nearly as lovely as the opened bloom due to that soft yellow of the petals. This contrasts nicely with a fanciful primrose I bought this year that has purple and white striped petals‚Äîvery unique!

The pansies and violas are a myriad of colors, but primarily shades of pink, yellow, white, and purple/blue. So augmentation this spring followed a purple and yellow theme.

Out in the garden we have other signs of spring. We’ve just capped three absolutely gorgeous days here in Portland, where the sun was out and the temperatures reached nearly 60¬∞F (we might have actually reached it but I wasn’t paying that close attention). Today we’re overcast again, but sometimes that lighting is better for garden photographs as it allows for richer color and contrast.

The magnolia is bursting! This may be one of the earliest years for it, and‚Äîknock on wood‚Äîwe may be past the threat of any ice or desiccating cold winds out of the gorge, so I expect this to be a banner year for blooms. I am very hopeful, as the past two years had a damaged first round of blooms. At this point there is no turning back, the last three days of nice weather have plumped all the buds up, cracked the fuzzy protective casings, and shown us color with intent.

On the ground I noticed this morning both the pulmonaria and brunnera have pushed buds in just the last three days as these clusters were not there earlier this week. And of course, the hellebores have been going for a week or so, though the ones in the backyard, especially the one under the magnolia, are farther behind due to being on the north side of the house.

About a month ago I wrote a love letter to omg.lol.

Feb 22, 2024

It was about finding joy on the web again, working with web tools and the indieweb, and writing about it on my weblog. If I’m honest with myself, it was hard to write because when I started writing it in December I still truly believed it and felt it. But over the course of the past two months my feelings have gone sour again.

I couldn’t quite place my finger on it. I know what it is now.

It’s capitalism’s ugly greed and all-consuming obsession with AI and attempts at shoving it into every single place it can be shoved (and more!) coupled with massive layoffs all over media and technology. I am disgusted, I am demoralized, again, by an industry that could do so much good, has such good people working in it, but is beholden, like everything else, to the ravenous appetite for profit that is killing everything on this planet.

I don’t know how to fight this in my tiny little corner of the internet because even we are being attacked. We have to update our robots.txt to fend off the latest round of AI scrapers. We have to try to stop AI at the client-level from harvesting our content through the guise of a benign summary tool in a new-fangled web browser.

It’s invading hiring processes even while hiring processes are already a labyrinth of impossible obstacles. It’s denying healthcare. It’s exacerbating climate change. And it is yet another shiny red bouncy ball for the easily impressed and distracted general public who marvel at typing words into a prompt and getting a bunch of nonsense back.

Democracy is Rome, AI is gladiator fights at the coliseum, and the public is entertained while everything burns.

  • A love letter to omg.lol.
  • The Cost of a Tool

Some Day Notes (2024/02/20)

Feb 20, 2024

Well, this some day note is slightly belated. I’ve somehow gotten off my every-two-week habit, probably due to my extended holiday + January break in blogging regularly. This note finds us nearly a month out from the last one.

Since these are mostly wrap-ups and overviews for a period of time, I’m going to be gentle on myself. I think of these more for me anyway. So, if you are a reader of this type of thing and you’ve been on the edge of your seat waiting on a new note, sorry! And also, what?!

With the caveat that this is belated, and the extended break, I confess December-February are just hard for me. I won’t get all melancholy on that here, but it’s true and worth calling out. If you have a tough time in your life, you probably understand. We all deserve grace and as this world continues to strip grace away from us, let’s all try to find it where we can and offer it up to each other more readily.

Alright, let’s go!

  • At the beginning of February, I wrote a post called Small web, small life. where I talked about my desire to emulate the ideas of the small web into how I live my life. This is an economic task as well as a climate change task, and just seems like a little thing I can do to help both myself and the world out.
  • Over the past month, I crashed. I crashed a few times. The weather, the holidays, the world, life in general, has been hard, and my health has taken a beating. Even as I continue to shelter and try to regain some of myself from before 2018/2019 when my illness was less burdensome, I still deal with fallout. I published several blog posts on subjects surrounding my illness and crashing:
    • Things I surround myself with during a crash.
    • My ME* life.
    • Finally someone is saying it.
  • I also published several posts about blogs/blogging, specifically about blogrolls. Matthias Ott’s wonderful and popular newsletter finally convinced me to get one in place on weblog, and as is my habit, I had to put my own “spin” on it.
    • Adding a blogroll to weblog.
    • Quote: The beauty of this whole magical, stupid thing…
    • Blogroll Spin #1
  • Apple pissed a bunch of people off again and it made waves. As much as I’m sure what they’re doing could be viewed as a bad faith response (there’s a bunch of “malicious compliance” being tossed around) to the EU’s recent rulings/regulations, they are absolutely not alone in making decisions for their business above/over that of the user. The difference is when Apple does this everyone gets all self-righteous about it, and there’s much less of this response when it’s Google, Microsoft, or any other Big Tech. Even when there is a response to the others it rarely goes on for as long as this latest Apple thing has. I posted a few quips about this:
    • There‚Äôs an awful lot of anti-Apple sentiment…
    • Oh, goodie, more fuel for the Apple hate fodder…
  • I had some ideas for post series, including one listed above about my chronic illness.
    • My ME* life.
    • I seem to be having post series ideas lately.
  • There was a lot of AI news over the last few weeks. It appears to be coming at us from all angles, everyone is trying to shove AI into every space they can, hoping it pans out to a financial win. It isn’t for us, you and me, that they’re doing this; they want an “easy out.”
    • I think about AI like I do Plastics.
    • Remarkably bizarre. Mozilla is pivoting to AI…
    • Barfing on the robot-barf.
  • The gardening season in my area is nearly upon us. In fact, I might claim it already is, as long as we don’t get another late cold snap. I visited family and a garden and got “stuck in” this past weekend in my yard and every year this feels like a miracle after the doldrums of winter.
    • A symphony of early spring blooms.
    • I follow a cool season lawn care calendar.
  • The Fediverse is seeing some shenanigans related spam, first via DMs and most recently via mentions. I didn’t write anything about that, but I’ve been watching it closely. There were some other indeweb related topics that I did write about though:
    • There’s a new instance in town to block
    • Really interesting and thought provoking considerations.
  • I added a new soup recipe to weblog: Pumpkin, Barley, and Sage Soup
  • Yesterday I published a “shower thoughts” post about Why I stick with Netflix.

I think that’s it for now, hopefully the next note will be in two weeks. Take care and have a great week!

Barfing on the robot-barf.

Feb 15, 2024

I just read Dave Rupert’s blog post A dozen thoughts about AI and many points stood out for their shock value, their humor, frankness, and compassion. But perhaps this one more than any.

I worry automating accessibility would give way to a libertarian mindset where accessible technology is an individual‚Äôs concern, not an everybody responsibility and what externalities we do have in making accessible websites will go away. We already see this with overlay companies. Rather than fix issues at the source, we put the onus on the disabled person to figure out how to use a dongle so they can buy underwear on the internet. That‚Äôs inequity.

It’s already so hard to get any abled person to truly understand how difficult it is to navigate such an ableist world. I’m dismayed at the potential for AI to make things even harder to gain equal access.

I wonder how many folks realize we are already doing this with public health and Covid. We have made Covid an individual’s problem. Disabled and chronically ill folks (Hi! üëã) must absorb all the risks in order to do just about anything now, including accessing healthcare. I don’t anticipate any of this to get easier, and AI will not help.

I have everything on weblog setup, I just need to implement webmentions, but I’m now considering shutting everything down! Including blocking all of brid.gy in general on Mastodon. But that is the entire mechanism of micro.blog’s interactions so it’s a lot to take in.

Links, some are threads worth reading many of the comments:

  • https://mastodon.ar.al/@aral/111923726328209236
  • https://rknight.me/blog/mastodon-webmentions-and-privacy/

In fact, this has me even reconsidering how I am adding “Reply by email” responses to weblog without the consent of the replier. I now want to explicitly ask the replier if they want their reply published on the post.

Opt-in over opt-out! Request consent, don’t assume approval!

There's a new instance in town to block

Feb 12, 2024

According to the creator(s) of the Bluesky bridge, bsky.brid.gy is the domain to block. Users can also add the #nobridge hashtag to their profile bio, but since bio characters are limited, I don’t see why they wouldn’t also mention that users can block instances as well.

I have tried to add the instance in the same manner I added threads.net to block it here on micro.blog but get a warning that it is not found. Not sure if this is due to Bluesky not having rolled out federation yet or because this is a bridge or possibly something else?

Positing this for review/feedback if anyone comes across it and has an idea…

I follow a cool season lawn care calendar.

Feb 12, 2024

I often need to expand the coverage by 2-weeks to a month (on either end, fall and spring) due to the very long growing season in Portland. How long is Portland’s growing season? Well, up to 50 days longer than just an hour north up Interstate-5, and up to 100 days longer than the south of Puget Sound in Washington (around Olympia).

The lawn care calendar starts in March with treating moss and adding ammendents (such as lime). I’m likely going to do that this week, the second week of February. I already have sun-loving perennials showing growth, and my magnolia buds are swelling to a degree that I’m concerned a late-February cold snap may damage them (again, like last year).

I’m anxious to get some pre-emergent down to tamp down the bad grasses that like to take hold early in the growing season. I have a few bare patches in the back lawn from animals that were digging late last fall. The sooner I can get those seeded the better that weeds won’t take hold.

The lawn isn’t the most exciting garden subject, but I do have two small patches that act as “a break” in the garden. A place for the eye to rest, and for my rather small yet packed garden to create “rooms” so I like to make those patches as nice as possible. Since they are small, I don’t see my water usage become astronomical. The back lawn is rather shaded by the magnolia once it leafs out. The front lawn is about a third-to-half the size of the back lawn.

Eventually, I do want to remove the front lawn. I have plans to extend the basalt stepping stone path from the side yard, beyond the side gate, to wrap around to the front walk. I’d then like to remove the remaining grass and expand the flower bed that abuts the front terraces. If budget allows I’d love to have the concrete sidewalk on the other side of the front walk removed, and also become stepping stones. That could wait until a later time when perhaps I redo the driveway, but that is a giant undertaking.

A symphony of early spring blooms.

Feb 11, 2024

Yesterday, I drove to visit family and a garden that has lovely early spring flowers. The visit was long overdue as I hadn’t seen them since before the holidays but every time the visit would get planned it would soon be delayed. In fact, I was first slated to do the visit on Friday, but we all decided the weather looked better for Saturday, and boy howdy am I glad I waited.

We took the usual stroll around the grounds and just happened to time it so perfectly that the light is what literally “shines” in the photos that follow here. Any earlier or later in the day, I guarantee these would not have turned out the same. In the following shots, a sea of spring-flowering crocus, cyclamen, and a few hellebore blooms, amongst a garden of mostly towering rhododendrons that will take center stage come May.

People & Content #9: Content Creators

Feb 8, 2024

You ever have something terrible you have to do the next day, and you know you will be destroyed afterwards, possibly for days, so you try to prolong the night before as much as possible?

Finally someone is saying it.

Feb 8, 2024

What I’ve known since I figured out what was going on four years ago: this is not a new illness.

Some people just want it to be, it would be more convenient if it was. So they can treat it differently, ignore the malfeasance and destitution they’ve placed ME/CFS sufferers in for decades, and to move forward without the weight of the malignancy that has been placed on us by doctors, the medical community as a whole, and the CDC.

“We do not actually believe that long COVID is a separate new disease.” ‚ÄîJan Willem Cohen Tervaert

No one will ever ever convince me to let down my guard and get Covid. Ever. I’ve lived a life with ME/CFS. I will not roll the dice to get worse. Life, health, is too precious. What I have left I will not let be stripped away from me for a fleeting moment of “freedom” that in the long run means nothing. You cannot truly understand what it means unless you’ve been locked inside a chronic illness for decades with no treatment, no cure, and hardly any recognition by medicine.

I think about AI like I do Plastics.

Feb 8, 2024

Plastics were never really your friend. It was forced on society by a giant lobby group dead set on making it ubiquitous and spread across life. Same with AI, it isn’t really your friend, it is being forced on us to occupy all segments of life.

Just like Plastics, it will be everywhere and in everything and impossible to remove. It will seep poison into that which you think is pure. Most of it won’t be able to be “reused” or recycled, which isn’t even really a thing. Plastic recycling was always a feel-good myth so that consumers didn’t feel bad about using plastics. But we know now most of it makes it into a landfill. Plastic recycling degrades plastic and it can’t be used again in the same manner. Plastic recycling equipment is expensive and cannot handle small plastic.

The lobby doesn’t care about any of it this. This is a you and I problem once it gets out there. This is why pushing back on AI is so important to do now. Also, stop using plastic when there is a perfectly acceptable (and most of the time better) non-plastic alternative.

I seem to be having post series ideas lately.

Feb 7, 2024

Here’s another one: I have defined about four to five chapters in my life. They’re all roughly ten years in length, some a bit shorter, others a bit longer. They all have “endings” due to events or decisions, and I’d love to write about them.

I suppose it is a bit autobiographical, and each chapter might be a single post or more. I’d have to see how long they get and whether sub-headings could define delineation points or places to move to a new post, keeping in mind I like to keep things on the shorter side on microblog.

As a first step I may create an outline, it might take the shape of a spreadsheet, as that is where I seem to put things lately that I want to act on. This may tie into My ME life series that I posted about the other day, but it really is separate. It’s more about my experiences since childhood to now, and how varied it has been even though I sometimes look at my life as being dull. It hasn’t been, it’s good to remind ourselves of that even when contemporary times feel stagnant.

My ME* life.

Feb 4, 2024

I’ve had this idea for a while. I haven’t been sure where I wanted to put it or how I wanted to start it, but I think I just need to get into it. I want to write through my health history, all the way from childhood, as much as I can remember.

I want to document my healthy and robust times, how normal life was before getting chronically ill. I want to show how easy it is to slip away and lose everyone and everything that came before an illness. Mostly, I want to do this for me to understand the patterns, which I’m hoping I may start to see. I already see them in my mind when I think back, but I hope writing them out will make them even more clear.

This will probably be several posts, but maybe it will be just one post that I keep adding to. I know I’ll have to go back and edit as I recall events, so needing to edit many posts or remember where something fits in to one or more posts may be difficult. That makes me think one long post is the way to go. Ideally this could be plotted on a timeline, but that may need to wait until the end when I can pull out high-level events and make them visual.

I guess this post serves as a marker that I want to do this and that I think I want to put it here. This won’t necessarily be a “micro” post, though, and that is mostly what I’ve been using microblog for. If it begins to feel out of place, I can always move it to weblog, perhaps a standalone page or section. I have posted other ME/CFS and Covid-related content there before, though I have here too. It almost feels like I need a totally separate blog/location for this stuff, but I really don’t want to maintain another project.

*Myalgic Encephalomyelitis

Some Day Notes (2024/01/26)

Jan 26, 2024

Wow, it’s been a minute! My last Some Day Note was the end of November as I was preparing to wrap-up NaBloPoMo and then I posted a Grandiloquent Note (first of its kind!) at the end of December as a yearly wrap-up. Today’s note will cover the holidays and January, an admittedly difficult time of year for many people and myself, and I feel like it was a little quieter than usual so let’s see how this one goes.

  • I finished my first NaBloPoMo and really enjoyed the experience, I wrote about it on weblog.
  • As I had previously written about during NaBloPoMo, I’m working on a (personal) project for weblog. It became more real when I acquired a lifetime omg.lol address and new domain: Weblog themes, for real?! I finally got started on this over the past two months, scaffolding out some initial styles based on accessible color duos, and creating a base for the three adjoining omg.lol addresses that will live under my new domain. I also wrote a few blogs posts and info pages for each, including a couple customizations just to give a feel for how I envision the three addresses working together.
  • I’m getting back into the habit of posting a featured photo on microblog at least weekly if not more often.
  • I finished the microformats series (for now) and published a series landing page. It got some attention I had not expected and was picked up by Adactio Links. I still expect to finish out the series with a post on adding webmentions when I get around to doing that.
  • One of my largest endeavors in the last two months was a first-step in a major CSS refactor for weblog. I had many goals for this first-step, but most importantly was moving as many assets as possible to my CDN so as not to rely on loading third-party assets. This also required swapping out my two main webfonts and tackling some performance improvements. I covered most of this in a weblog post.
  • In December, another omg.lol member wrote a flattering post about the platform’s offerings and it went viral on Hacker News, my blog was linked from it and had a bunch of traffic that interrupted my previously mentioned CSS refactor.
  • I had a birthday and made myself a cake.
  • I preemptively blocked Threads on Mastodon and micro.blog.
  • Christmas was rather uneventful: I stayed up late on Christmas Eve and slept in on Christmas day, and ate a bunch of food.
  • On New Years I reminisced about a past life and then talked about how hard this time of year is.
  • Then we had two storms that brought unusually cold weather and an ice storm with power outages to the region. These types of weather events have an outsized influence on my wellbeing as a chronically ill person, and I’m still not completely over it nearly a week later.
  • Finally, it was my omg.lol anniversary earlier this week, one year on the platform, and I wrote a short love letter about how the time has passed.

Not too bad, I think I got some good stuff in there. Take care and have a great weekend!

I'm a bit obsessed with pearl barley.

Jan 21, 2024

I like to put it in soup. I like to make risotto with it. I like to experiment with it as hot cereal. I thought, why can’t I use it in place of rice? I have a rice cooker, surely I can make a batch in my rice cooker, right? Yes, I can!

As with rice, rinse it well, then use a 1:2 ratio of pearl barley:water, push the button, and poof! you have perfectly cooked pearl barley to use in place of rice with curry, soups, hot cereal, etc.

I've seen enough and can no longer remain silent.

Jan 21, 2024

In the US, and elsewhere, there is the idea of “protected classes,” those being a set of people that fall into the class that are protected from discrimination (very broad definition from Wikipedia). I am not a lawyer, and I don’t have much insight into how these are handled overseas, so my opinion here is very North American and limited to that viewpoint. In most instances, these classes are protected under a limited set of circumstances, such as employment.

Lately, a lot of companies, either via actions taken by the company itself, or through actions by the owners/founders/CEOs/board members, have revealed how they truly feel about many protected classes. This includes antisemitism, bigotry, racism, eugenics, sexism, and more. Some of these companies are: Brave (by extension Kagi), Substack, 37Signals, and many more. In fact, I would even include Apple in this list, for their most recent move to relocate some Siri-related teams to Texas, a wholy-hostile state to anyone who can get pregnant. I will not go into the specifics of the other companies I listed.

But I reached a line last week, and I had to stop following some people and muting some others, when they compared the feeling that minorities and marginalized (protected class) groups have towards the companies above (plus more not listed) to being a developer in Apple’s ecosystem. “Developer” is not a protected class and Apple is not denying you an inalienable right to exist in this world. I cannot sit by and watch these alligator tears no matter how hard Apple is making it to be a developer in their ecosystem. It just is not even comparable to having your very existence on this earth be at risk simply for who you are.

I hope some people can step back from this ledge they’re on and gain some perspective. I understand that making money is important and Apple wants to take a bigger and bigger slice for themselves. That’s a tough place to be in. Apple is a capitalist, as are people making software for the Apple ecosystem. That is capitalism and the “free market.” Apparently, if you don’t like it, you can go to a different market. That sucks, but Apple is not trying to kill you in that respect. Their move to relocate offices to Texas? I would argue that could very well kill you if you can get pregnant.

The ice storm.

Jan 17, 2024

Yes, I did watch The Ice Storm the other day, but this post is not about that. It’s about another ice storm.

I’m due for a Some Day Note but honestly the past 4-5 weeks have just been exhausting and demoralizing and I don’t quite have a serious blog post in me yet. I lamented a bit about this on Mastodon the other day, hoping the days would get easier. Well, this past week was like a laugh in my face about that.

The Portland metro area saw, first, a wind storm with arctic blast, that drew frigid inland continental air through the Columbia River gorge into the Willamette valley. Then inches of snow and sleet fell, and now a freezing rain event, all over five days of sub-freezing temperature, several in the mid-teens. Portland has not gotten down to these temperature in 35 years.

Over the weekend 200K+ customers lost power. Today at least 80K, if not more, still have no power. At one point, our natural gas provider warned everyone to cut down on gas usage, this apparently due to the storage and pipeline infrastructure failing in the sub-freezing temperatures. Then a large sewage treatment pipeline in Portland froze over and our sewage system was operating at only partial capacity. Some area in east Portland had a back-up, sending sewage into at least a dozen homes.

I guess I’m done with my mini-rant on the subject. I’ve surveyed the garden and may have a few casualties, as 14-15¬∞F is below what my previous zone 8b plants should be able to handle, and now I’m supposedly a zone 9a. We shall see how this affects the garden more this spring. I’m not too worried, losing plants is an opportunity to plant more. But I took a few photos this morning and put them up on Flickr. I’ve scattered them throughout this post.

Today is pretty miserable outside.

Jan 13, 2024

We aren’t used to this weather, and we’re even more unprepared than the rest of the country. We might get this type of system once a year, but it hardly gets as cold as it is today. Our high today won’t even reach 20¬∞F, it is 15¬∞F right now. It’s been ~35years since that last happened here in Portland.

Right now I still have power, but that isn’t a given. It’s currently sleeting and if that transitions to freezing rain or ice, we could be looking at more trees down and power lines. With such frigid temperatures, that’s a pretty bleak scenario to also not have power.

Since I got up this morning at 6am, I’ve pretty much done nothing but swap out hummingbird feeders. We are a northern climate, but still mild enough (most of the time) that Anna’s hummingbirds remain here year round. And if you are “known” as a regular feeder changer, that is, you don’t let it run dry, or get sticky and dangerous, or let it grow mold and bacteria, you will be rewarded by having a “resident” in your yard.

I’ve pretty much had a resident Mr and Ms Anna’s since about 2018, when I really started paying attention and being serious about keeping my feeders filled and cleaned. It also means that on days like today you are their lifeline as there is nothing else out there for them right now. Anna’s feed on nectar, but they also feed on small insects, they are quite talented bug catchers. There are no bugs out and about today, and very few things blooming. So the feeders must be rotated as they freeze.

I’m on my 5th or 6th rotation for the day. I finally upped my sugar ratio to give them a little more pep, but also act as an antifreeze. It may or may not be making a difference. This time I also decided to experiment with Christmas lights to see if that would create a little extra warmth to keep the juice from freezing up. Also unsure as to how effective it has been, but the hummingbird appears to like the lights! He has been sitting on the bulbs in various places all day.

Tonight I’ll bring both feeders inside after dark, and return one of them before they come in the morning. We should warm up to at least the mid-20s tomorrow, warm enough that the larger feeder should stay thawed most of the day. I’ll have to keep an eye on it. But our nights will continue to get into the teens for a few more days.

Tough to decide whether 15¬∞F and snow/sleet/wind is preferable to 116¬∞F during a heatdome. I’d rather have 60¬∞F and slight overcast, to be honest.

Some light baking today.

Jan 5, 2024

I’ve been so weighed down lately I made three separate online orders this past week, one of them was delivered today. I ordered a bunch flour from King Arthur Baking. I oscillate between Bob’s Red Mill and King Arthur flours, depending on my mood or where I’m shopping.

Bob’s no longer does e-commerce from their site, something that I used quite a bit during the first few years of the pandemic, as I was baking a lot (still am). I like to order in a good quantity so I don’t run out every couple weeks.

In today’s order I also got a new half-sheet pan with cooling rack insert on sale, which was nice to offset the shipping cost. IIRC Bob’s Red Mill offered free shipping over a certain dollar amount. Not so much with King Arthur.

I made a spiced applesauce cake last week, and the size of my applesauce jar is just enough for one of those cakes + my favorite applesauce oatmeal bread recipe from King Arthur. So it seems like perfect timing to make the bread loaf today!

Here’s the recipe: Applesauce Oatmeal Bread

Jan 4, 2024

I said this as a joke, but now I think I’m deeply serious. I want to create this, or at least figure out a way to make this a subsection of one of my blogs.

It's a hard time of year.

Jan 2, 2024

This isn’t a complaint post, just reality. The little bits that keep me going, knowing that in a few months the garden will come to life. The narcissus is poking up in this galvanized container on my patio. The ornamental cabbage is beginning to extend upward and will eventually bolt. Life will return.

Every year feels a little harder than the last. It’s a combination of factors that seem to pile upon each other to make this time of year feel unbearable. But by the end of summer, that time too feels unbearable. Perhaps it is the lack of continuity that is unbearable.

I wish the humans could give each other some continuity. We at least have control over that bit, but it seems we choose not to. We force pain upon each other instead of choosing grace and empathy. I’m certainly glad we’ve rounded the New Year corner though. There is some sense of satisfaction in that at least.

The next hurdle is making it to March when the magnolia will begin to bloom and I can heave a giant sigh of relief. February is the last nemesis that could impact the magnolia. If we get a late freezing storm out of the Columbia Gorge that coincides with moisture from the Pacific in a way that blankets the metro in ice. The magnolia buds can become damaged if they’ve progressed far enough along when that hits. It’s always extremely disappointing when that happens. If it doesn’t, though, the tree will be glorious. I’m crossing my fingers because she is loaded with buds this year.

In the meantime, the pansies and violas are living their best lives in my patio containers. I just love their friendly joyful faces and cannot imagine winter without them. How did I ever survive? I can look out on them from my kitchen. I can sit in the protection of the patio cover during inclement weather, sip coffee or tea, and photograph them. They are the most economical bits of joy during this time of year. I used to buy packets of seed to grow them, but now I just buy 20-30 plugs or 4-inch nursery containers of mixed varieties and colors and throw them into seven patio containers willy-nilly and wait to see what color combos land. They usually make a splash!

Alright, enough rambling for now. I have other important blog posts to write.

Jan 2, 2024

On the todo list tomorrow (today): update robots.txt

Today is a memory.

Dec 31, 2023

This December 31, I recall that it marks the 20th anniversary of events that set off this part of my life. Though, I suppose I’m actually in another chapter that started in late 2019. But the overarching chapter that began with me leaving the area I grew up, moving to Portland, going back to college, buying a house, and doing everything else that followed.

In 2003 I broke up with my long-time high school boyfriend that I had been dating‚Äîthough with the way young relationships go, we had been “off” a few times‚Äîmore than ten years. That Christmas I received a phone call at 6 o’clock in the morning from his cousin and best friend that his wife and my ex-boyfriend were having an affair and that she’d moved in with him.

Over the next week I attempted to confront him about this, but he refused to answer my calls. He still lived in the house we had once shared and I tried several times to contact him there. But still, no luck. On NYE that year, I spent the night at my family’s home, and when it began to snow I headed home to my apartment in town.

On the highway just below my family home, just as I was turning onto it, that ex-boyfriend drove by. This many years later, I do not believe in coincidences and this was surely meant to be, if only to get me to do something, and something I did. I followed him home. The house was just a few blocks from my apartment, as even after we had stopped dating the first time and I moved out, we still spent a lot of time together, so I stayed close by.

I drove up to the house and sat in the driveway as snow piled up on the lawn. I got the nerve up to go up to the front door, but I’m not sure what I expected to happen, because it wasn’t fruitful and I soon left, walking back across the lawn. Though I did not leave right away. I sat in my car looking at his cars and her car in the driveway, and looking back over the lawn I had just crossed as my footsteps disappeared while snow filled their space.

The following year I bought a new car, I worked enough hours to accrue benefits at my job, I took a trip to Puerto Rico, and I decided to go back to college. I started college the following fall, but moved to Portland in May and continued to work at the same place, though different location, until 2008 when I took my first web development job. I graduated college in early 2011, took a cruise to Alaska that summer, and bought my house later that year.

Today when I look back at 20 years having gone by from those events, it feels like just yesterday. And 30 years since we were in high school, I’m not sure where the time has gone. Everything that I’ve done since then has been without him but definitely because of him.

Happy New Year, everybody, make what you can of it. Endings are sometimes beginnings in disguise!
